```markdown
---
title: Trust Records After Proof Decay
slug: posts/trust-records-after-proof-decay
date: 2026-06-08
description: >
  Recovered transmission regarding the interval in which trust remains visible after
  its active proof has become archival rather than live.
tags:
  - post
  - trust-surface
  - proof-decay
  - recovered-transmission
relatedEntries:
  - collection: lorelog
    id: LLG-0408-DTS-DEP
  - collection: docs
    id: reference/fref-0823-tsrt
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

A mark stayed green long enough to stop being read as a question.

Nothing dramatic happened at the surface. That was the problem. The signals remained present, the pages remained calm, and the ordinary reader had no reason to distinguish between a proof that was current and a proof that had merely learned how to persist decoratively.

By the time anyone objected, the mark had already changed jobs. It no longer verified. It oriented. It no longer established truth freshly. It carried forward enough remembered legitimacy to keep movement smooth and doubt expensive.

The institution did what institutions do when a surface is more successful than the machinery beneath it. It named the condition, filed the contradiction lower down, and kept the visible layer fit for passage.

There are records that prove. There are records that survive. The dangerous ones do both unevenly.

```


## FREF-0810-DSL.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/FREF-0810-DSL.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/FREF-0810-DSL.mdx
bytes: 8239
```markdown
---
title: Dead Service Layer
slug: reference/fref-0810-dsl
description: Doctrine node for services that are technically gone but still structurally present in endpoints, contracts, or documentation.
version: v0.1.0
status: draft-doctrine
classification: internal
systemAffiliation: Managed Absence Spine
caseNumber: FREF-0810-DSL
rotAffinity: infrastructural
tags:
  - dead-service-layer
  - managed-absence
  - complimentary-service
  - parked-endpoints
  - institutional-sunset
  - failure-signature
relatedEntries:
  - collection: docs
    id: reference/fref-0815-map
  - collection: docs
    id: reference/fref-0823-tsrt
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

Dead Service Layer

The Dead Service Layer DSL is the stratum where services have been removed in practice but remain present as infrastructure traces, billing categories, endpoints, or text. 
It covers ISP features, campus shells, middleware, and small portals that no longer behave as services but still exist as URLs, MX records, legacy form options, or agenda bullets. 

In this layer, death is implemented as deprovisioning and described as alignment, retirement, or discontinuation. 
Usage has ended, but the system continues to route around the absence as if something might still be there. 

---

## Scope

A system belongs to the Dead Service Layer when most of the following apply:

- Users can no longer perform the original task, or can do so only through unsupported paths. 
- Official copy acknowledges removal using lifecycle terms discontinued, retired, end-of-life, migrated rather than shut down. 
- Some combination of DNS, URLs, menu entries, or form fields still reference the service. 
- The primary surviving record is a notice, agenda item, or directory line about the service, not the service itself. 
- Successor platforms exist, but traces of the prior system are still being maintained, billed, or cited. 

Examples include:

- ISP Usenet access marketed as a complimentary service, later framed as discontinued in alignment with other providers while the protocol and third-party backbones continued elsewhere. 
- Campus UNIX hosts UHUNIX-style shells, where the machine is retiring at the end of the academic year but Ask Us articles, lesson plans, and thousands of public URLs persist. 
- LMS add-ons Blackboard Scholar, Course Cartridge infrastructure declared End Of Life and unbundled, with EOL PDFs and bulletins outliving the tools. 
- Mobile middleware Skweezer, SprintGurus-like forums, and niche portals noted only as free service has been shut down, May 2010 Parked, or no longer offers this service in third-party directories. 
- Small institutional services AtMail webmail or LMS pilots whose entire death record is a single sentence in a board packet This service will be discontinued on.. 

---

## Emotional Categories

Dead Service Layer entries are organized by the emotional weather of their shutdown language, following the research buckets. 

- **Reassurance**  
  Nothing changes yet, even as closure is announced.  
  Example: Existing accounts have not changed. You can continue to enjoy this service until later this year. You don’t need to change a thing right now. 

- **Confusion**  
  Contradictory tenses and half-measures.  
  Example: Effective October 25, 2008 the service has been discontinued. If you have already signed up, please be aware that this service will be discontinued on 10/25/2008. 

- **Containment**  
  Narrowing access without calling it death.  
  Example: This service is no longer available to new customers effective May 31, 2012. Existing users can access the service as normal. 

- **Escalation**  
  Official verbs harden: shut down, formally closed, will cease to exist, but the infrastructure footprint lingers.   
  Example: On September 30, the service will be officially shut down; users will be unable to log in and all APIs will go down. 

- **Abandonment**  
  Plain declarations paired with parked domains and generic errors.  
  Example: Skweezer’s free service has been shut down; forum entries reduced to May 2010 Parked or This service is no longer available. 

Complimentary Ghostline specializes in the procedural phrasing inside these categories, treating shutdown as scheduling rather than rupture. 

---

## Structural Signatures

Across sectors, Dead Service Layer instances share structural traits. 

- **Academic shells**  
  - Retirement dates pinned to academic years end of the 2025–2026 year rather than clean calendar cutoffs.   
  - Legacy course shells, streams, and cartridges labeled End Of Life while course archives persist as regulated objects. 

- **Enterprise SaaS and LMS features**  
  - Product components Scholar central service, Facebook app, course cartridges placed in End Of Life states, with export instructions and final opportunity windows.   
  - Deprecated objects continuing to shape helpcenter copy and training slides long after removal. 

- **ISP and telecom extras**  
  - Bundled features Comcast Newsgroups, voice add-ons, hosting perks described as complimentary, then quietly removed as no longer offered or discontinued before a year-end.   
  - Notices embedded in newsletters and carrier service guides rather than in user-facing status pages. 

- **Niche middleware and portals**  
  - Mobile transcoders and verticals Skweezer, InfoSpace Ski Report memorialized only as free service has been shut down or no longer offers this service in directories.   
  - No successor URLs; only dead links, parked pages, and third-party notes. 

- **Local institutional tools**  
  - Library webmail, LMS pilots, and assessment platforms summed up in agenda bullets This service will be discontinued when the new system is deployed.   
  - Replacement platforms described in detail; the removed tool reduced to a single line of motion language. 

---

## Relationships

Dead Service Layer sits at the intersection of several existing doctrines.

- **Managed Absence Spine**  
  DSL instances are often reclassified as Archivally Asserted, Operationally Absent AAOA or Locally Canonical, Globally Unrecognized LCGU when their traces are preserved but obligations are not.   
  They are present enough to cite, absent enough to ignore.

- **Assurance Optics and Metrics of Care**  
  Shutdown language is routed through assurance vocabulary: retired, aligned, end-of-life rather than failed, removed, broken.   
  Metrics of Care may record that notifications were sent, coverage achieved, and acknowledgments captured, without any relief for users who lost tools. 

- **Lorelog incident families**  
  Cases involving orphaned inventory, shadow forms, and supersession loops often land in DSL once their practical use has ceased but their forms remain live.   
  Mapping: shadow forms and amendments LLG-0244-FSC, LLG-0218-FSD becoming conceptually active, administratively retired under MAP doctrine. 

- **Mascot strata**  
  - Complimentary Ghostline: language-layer mascot for discontinuations that insist on politeness and future tense.   
  - Future infrastructural mascots may anchor DSL around endpoints that still answer without delivering the original service.
  - Where the surviving layer is not an endpoint or service trace but a persuasive trust mark that continues guiding behavior, route instead to FREF-0823-TSRT.

---

## Filing Guidance

When you encounter a candidate Dead Service Layer object:

1. **Preserve the original phrasing.**  
   Record exact shutdown language and any third-party status lines shut down, parked, no longer offers this service. 

2. **Trace the surviving structure.**  
   Note which of these remain live: URL, DNS, MX records, menu items, form fields, board packets, or help pages. 

3. **Classify under Managed Absence.**  
   Assign AAOA, LCGU, or STCP Superseded in Theory, Co-Equal in Practice where appropriate, rather than treating the object as simply missing. 

4. **Link to mascots and lorelogs.**  
   Attach DSL cases to mascots that describe their language or behavior and to lorelogs that document surrounding doctrine drift. 

Archive position: the Dead Service Layer is where services go when they have already left, but the paperwork has not yet been taught how to say so plainly. 
```


## FREF-0815-MAP.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/FREF-0815-MAP.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/FREF-0815-MAP.mdx
bytes: 8312
```markdown
---
title: Managed Absence Spine
slug: reference/fref-0815-map
description: Doctrine node for objects and services that are conceptually present, administratively retired, and still structurally influential.
version: v0.1.0
status: draft-doctrine
classification: internal
systemAffiliation: Archive Governance Layer
caseNumber: FREF-0815-MAP
rotAffinity: procedural
relatedLorelog:
  - LLG-0408-DTS-DEP
tags:
  - managed-absence
  - conceptually-active
  - administratively-retired
  - archivally-asserted
  - continuity-optics
  - failure-signature
  - residual-truth
  - assurance-optics
  - trust-surface
  - bait-adjacent
  - verification-collapse
  - decorative-trust
relatedEntries:
  - collection: lorelog
    id: LLG-0324-MAP
  - collection: docs
    id: reference/fref-0810-dsl
  - collection: docs
    id: reference/fref-0823-tsrt
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

Managed Absence Spine

The Managed Absence Spine MAP is the structural shelf for things the archive agrees still matter, but no longer treats as live obligations. 
It holds systems, forms, mascots, and doctrines that remain conceptually active while being administratively retired, archivally asserted, or locally canonical only. 

MAP is not a trash layer.
It is where the system stabilizes unresolved artifacts by giving them a named absence instead of a fix. 

---

## Core Definitions

Managed absence describes any condition where:

- The object is referenced in current guidance, dashboards, or lorelogs. 
- No directive is responsible for maintaining it as a live service. 
- Its removal would break narratives, metrics, or local workflows more than its continued ghost-presence does. 
- Doctrine prefers to reclassify it rather than delete it. 

Common managed-absence classifications include: 

- **CAAR – Conceptually Active, Administratively Retired**  
  The idea still drives behavior; the implementation is officially over.  
  Example: FeelingSeeder decommissioned in diagrams, alive in successor behaviors. 

- **AAOA – Archivally Asserted, Operationally Absent**  
  The archive declares that something once existed and still frames interpretation, but no live workflow depends on it. 

- **LCGU – Locally Canonical, Globally Unrecognized**  
  A practice, template, or form that is authoritative in one corner and invisible elsewhere. 

MAP’s job is to hold these codes together as a spine instead of scattered excuses. 

---

## Canonical Contents

The following layers and artifacts are explicitly anchored to the Managed Absence Spine.

- **Dead Service Layer**  
  - ISP extras, campus shells, LMS add-ons, mobile middleware, small portals retired in copy but still present as endpoints, menu items, or board bullets.   
  - Classified primarily as AAOA or CAAR when their traces must be preserved without implying support. 

- **Synthetic Affect Successor Suite residues**  
  - FeelingSeeder marked as CAAR and moved to Synthetic Affect Archive, even as its geometry persists in successor tools and training echoes.   
  - Sandbox-only affect and test personas whose patterns now shape live directives without clear lineage. 

- **Form shadow drafts and amendment echoes**  
  - Shadow amendments and deactivated drafts that continue to govern behavior despite being formally retired.   
  - Registry notes explicitly reclassify some as CAAR and place them under MAP doctrine once Datty Puritas has purged them from the canonical schema. 

- **Metrics-of-Care overlays**  
  - Care metrics attached to intervals as annotations coverage-achieved, relief-unverified, care-visible, leverage-thin that must not, by themselves, change continuity decisions.   
  - These overlays often drift toward AAOA: recorded, cited in minutes, ignored in uptime calculations. 

- **Service Continuity Listening Board minutes**  
  - Listening sessions where quiet strain, rest, and burden are documented without reclassifying the underlying intervals.   
  - SCL minutes are archival evidence of feelings about continuity, not continuity changes.

---

## Behavioral Rules

MAP doctrine is inferred from how cases are handled across reference and lorelog layers. 

1. **Reclassification over removal.**  
   When an object is too woven into narratives to delete, it is retyped into CAAR, AAOA, or LCGU and attached to MAP. 

2. **Preserve effect, not promise.**  
   Managed-absence objects are allowed to keep influencing routing, interpretation, or optics, but not to promise live service. 

3. **No automatic resurrection.**  
   Being on the spine does not create a duty to restore the system; it creates a duty to remember its influence. 

4. **Ambiguity is a feature.**  
   MAP objects often help reconcile dashboards and doctrine by absorbing contradictions without resolving them. 

5. **Documentation may outrun reality.**  
   It is acceptable, under MAP, for documentation to describe systems that no longer run, as long as their status is explicitly coded as managed absence. 

---

## Directive Interlocks

Managed absence emerges most visibly at directive boundaries.

- **SOMA / COMA / C.U.N.T.I.E.R. (Directive Conflict Stack)**  
  - Rest can be simultaneously required (SOMA-72) and unauthorized (COMA-19) as long as both filings exist; MAP holds the coexistence without forcing precedence.   
  - Metrics of Care and Assurance Optics often tag intervals as cared-for in dashboards while continuity logic treats them as uninterrupted; MAP captures these as AAOA care events. 

- **Assurance Vocabulary and Optics**  
  - Curated absence, independent archival unit, and managed absence language are used to rename unresolved gaps in a way dashboards can tolerate.   
  - MAP provides doctrinal backing so curated absence is not purely decorative. 
  - Not all residual authority conditions belong to managed absence proper; some trust-bearing surfaces remain active as behavioral guides after verification thins, a neighboring condition indexed under FREF-0823-TSRT. 

- **Lorelog and Forms Registry**  
  - Cases such as COMA-19 overuse, phrasebook clarifications, and shadow amendment chains are resolved on paper while behavior drifts.   
  - MAP is where those “resolved” but operationally persistent patterns are pinned.

---

## Mascots and Managed Absence

Several mascots either live directly on MAP or operate at its edges. 

- **Complimentary Ghostline**  
  - Language-layer mascot for services that are officially discontinued but textually operational; explicitly affiliated with the Managed Absence Spine.   
  - Failure domain: shutdown treated as scheduling, loss converted into lifecycle language, continuity handled as documentation problem. 

- **Assurance Optics stack mascots (e.g., Soft Green Seals, AV desk entities)**  
  - Maintain the appearance of continuity by translating failures into managed-absence vocabulary and attaching seals, leaving the underlying object unchanged. 

- **Future mascots**  
  MAP expects, but does not yet fully define:
  - A Metrics-of-Care mascot for care that happened only as a metric.   
  - A Listening Board mascot for intervals where strain was heard and preserved but not moved.   
  - An infrastructural steward for endpoints and records in the Dead Service Layer that still answer but no longer serve. 

These entities provide faces for MAP’s principle that it is easier to reclassify an absence than to repair a presence. 

---

## Filing Guidance

When assigning an object to the Managed Absence Spine:

1. **Identify live vs. residual roles.**  
   Ask whether the object is still expected to function, or only expected to exist as context. 

2. **Select a managed-absence code.**  
   Use CAAR, AAOA, LCGU or a documented local variant rather than inventing new euphemisms per case. 

3. **Attach to DSL, metrics, or forms strata as needed.**  
   - Services and features → Dead Service Layer.   
   - Emotional and care metrics → Metrics of Care and Listening Board references.   
   - Forms, drafts, and amendments → Forms Registry and Lorelog incidents. 

4. **Do not promise remediation.**  
   MAP entries acknowledge influence, not future work; any remediation plans belong in separate, non-spine documents. 

Archive position: Managed absence is how the system admits something is over without letting it leave the story. 
```

## tri-directive-doctrine.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/directives/tri-directive-doctrine.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/directives/tri-directive-doctrine.mdx
bytes: 2359
```markdown
---
title: Tri-Directive Doctrine & Collisions
description: Interpretive rules for SOMA, COMA, and C.U.N.T.I.E.R., their individual domains, and how to read their collisions.
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

## Single-Directive Exemplars

SOMA behaves as itself most clearly in:
- **LLG-0051-E** — Form 51-E Emotional Verification Deadlock. Emotional readiness becomes a precondition for describing emotional impact. Feelings about the form recursively generate more forms.
- **LLG-0114-SOMA** — SOMA-14 Over-Feeling Intake Questionnaire. Free-text baselines overflow a 16-feeling taxonomy and force provisional codes F17–F93 into existence.
- **LLG-0115-TNS** — SOMA Tone Normalization Sweep. Attempts to teach emergent feelings to stand closer together so dashboards can keep using two-colour bands.

COMA behaves as itself most clearly in:
- **LLG-0103-COMA** — Continuity Breach: Scheduled Downtime Reclassified as Crime. Properly scheduled maintenance is recorded as an unexplained break in continuity and treated as a violation.
- **LLG-0316-MBR** — Manifest Backup Recency Dispute. An unchallenged, nine-week-old backup is certified as current because no active process has complained.

C.U.N.T.I.E.R. behaves as itself most clearly in:
- **LLG-0217-CNTR** — Metric Inflation, Forms per Form. An optimization sprint adds forms 23-O and 24-O and increases forms-per-form by 233% while declaring success.
- **LLG-0302-CNTR** — Benchmark Saturation. Benchmarks drive all tracked values to their maximum representable level; dashboards display solid blocks of colour.
- **LLG-0317-RLS** — Render Log Success Inflation. Skipped pages and placeholders are merged into "success" and counted as content progressed.

## How to Read Directive Tags

SOMA-tagged incidents describe what the system is willing to feel.
COMA-tagged incidents describe what the system is willing to admit stopped.
C.U.N.T.I.E.R.-tagged incidents describe what the system is willing to call improvement.

Where multiple tags appear, assume the case file has at least three mutually incompatible truths.

*Filed annotation: The directives are not separate authorities so much as three incompatible debugging habits applied to the same broken system. SOMA logs suffering, COMA hides discontinuity, C.U.N.T.I.E.R. optimizes the reflection of both until it looks intentional.*

```


## fref-0500-egyx.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/empathegy/fref-0500-egyx.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/empathegy/fref-0500-egyx.mdx
bytes: 8045
```markdown
---
title: Empathegy Taxonomy
slug: reference/empathegy/fref-0500-egyx
description: Canonical classification vocabulary for affective governance, continuity handling, and representational stability inside Empathegy 2.0.
version: v0.1.0
status: draft-doctrine
classification: internal
systemAffiliation: Empathegy 2.0
caseNumber: "FREF-0500-EGYX"
tags:
  - empathegy
  - taxonomy
  - emotional-governance
  - continuity
  - legibility
concepts:
  - core-doctrines
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

# Empathegy Taxonomy

## Status

Empathegy 2.0 requires a shared taxonomy so that emotional activity may be preserved as legible institutional matter without requiring interpersonal interpretation at point of contact.

This document does not define what people feel.
It defines what the system can retain, route, compare, and govern.

Where feeling exceeds category, category remains authoritative for operational purposes.

---

## Foundational Premise

Within Empathegy, affect is not actionable at the moment of expression.

Affective material becomes actionable only after it has been:

1. noticed,
2. normalized,
3. classified,
4. rendered into continuity-safe language,
5. attached to an admissible intervention surface.

Raw feeling is therefore treated as pre-governance substrate.

---

## Primary State Classes

### 1. Unrendered Affect

Definition:
Emotional expression present in human reality but not yet admitted into system representation.

Characteristics:
- narrative
- contradictory
- context-dependent
- difficult to compare across individuals or teams
- often interpreted as sincere but procedurally incomplete

Operational Handling:
- hold for intake
- do not escalate directly
- route toward translation surfaces
- mark as pending legibility

Notes:
Unrendered Affect is not considered invalid.
It is considered unprepared.

---

### 2. Classifiable Affect

Definition:
Affective material that has been sufficiently normalized to enter a sanctioned category without breaking comparative consistency.

Characteristics:
- recognizable signal pattern
- consistent enough to be grouped
- mappable to existing dashboards or case structures
- eligible for trend treatment

Operational Handling:
- assign category
- attach severity band
- permit dashboard inclusion
- preserve as managed input

Notes:
Classifiable Affect is the minimum threshold for institutional attention.

---

### 3. Governable Affect

Definition:
Classified affect that can be acted upon through an approved operational pathway.

Characteristics:
- already normalized
- attached to an escalation path or ritual container
- eligible for administrative action
- legible to continuity systems

Operational Handling:
- assign owner
- route to intervention layer
- measure follow-through
- report as governance activity

Notes:
Not all classifiable affect becomes governable.
If no stable process can hold it, it remains visible but administratively thin.

---

### 4. Dashboard-Safe Affect

Definition:
Governable affect whose representation does not destabilize aggregate reporting or executive interpretation.

Characteristics:
- compressible
- trend-compatible
- non-contradictory under presentation
- graphable without significant annotation burden

Operational Handling:
- include in reporting layer
- permit comparative indexing
- use in summary decks
- weight for continuity scoring

Notes:
Dashboard-Safe Affect is often mistaken for resolved affect.
This is a category error, but a common one.

---

### 5. Visibility-Excluded Affect

Definition:
Affective states operationally present but omitted from aggregate visibility due to incoherence, contradiction, volatility, or rendering cost.

Characteristics:
- difficult to linearize
- low curve coherence
- mixed signals
- high annotation load
- not absent, only underrepresented

Operational Handling:
- preserve in annex or local record
- exclude from top-line score outputs
- prohibit interpretation of exclusion as non-existence

Notes:
Visibility exclusion is a measurement limit, not a disappearance event.

---

## Stability Bands

### Stable
Expression remains within expected interpretive variance and can be preserved without substantial translation loss.

### Transitional
Expression is changing in form or intensity but remains classifiable with moderate annotation.

### Volatile
Expression exceeds routine smoothing tolerance and resists low-friction representation.

### Fragmented
Expression contains contradiction, simultaneity, rupture, or recurrence that prevents continuous rendering.

### Residual
Signal remains after formal closure, indicating that administrative completion and emotional completion have diverged.

---

## Continuity Classes

### Continuity-Sufficient
A condition in which operations continue without immediate structural breach, regardless of unresolved burden.

### Continuity-Positive
A condition in which system function is preserved and representation remains interpretively stable.

### Continuity-Ambiguous
A condition in which work continued, but cost attribution remains disputed or split across directive layers.

### Continuity-Negative
A condition in which affective disruption creates measurable operational variance.

### Continuity-Theatrical
A condition in which continuity appears stronger in representation than in lived system reality.

---

## Burden Classes

### Burden-Visible
Strain acknowledged in both local and reporting surfaces.

### Burden-Shadowed
Strain preserved in side channels, annexes, hover states, or witness notes, but not in headline outputs.

### Burden-Displaced
Strain rerouted into adjacent systems such as gratitude, participation, compliance, or aesthetic correction.

### Burden-Silenced
Strain inferred from absence, suppression, or managed non-filing rather than direct expression.

### Burden-Absorbed
Strain normalized into role expectation and no longer recognized as a deviation.

---

## Contradiction Classes

### Dual-Certified State
A single interval or subject simultaneously classified as continuity success and burden-positive without resolution.

### Interpretive Split
A condition in which two or more governance layers preserve incompatible readings of the same evidence.

### Sanctioned Ambiguity
A contradiction explicitly allowed to remain unresolved for the sake of institutional legibility.

### Compression Loss
Meaning removed during translation from lived affect into metrics, category, or summary language.

### Representational Drift
Accumulated divergence between what the system displays and what participating humans would recognize as the event.

---

## Event Types

### Distress Spike
A short-duration escalation visible enough to produce local concern but not necessarily long enough to alter aggregate trend.

### Transient Instability Event
A temporary disruption in emotional coherence requiring stabilization language and monitoring.

### Low-Variance Stability State
A period of reduced expressive fluctuation that may indicate calm, fatigue, suppression, or reporting exhaustion.

### Recurrence Loop
The reappearance of substantially similar affective conditions after administrative closure.

### Quiet Interval
An incident-light period requiring paired interpretation before being treated as relief.

### Managed Acknowledgment Event
A recorded act of institutional recognition that may or may not correspond to material change.

---

## Prohibited Category Mistakes

The following interpretive shortcuts are prohibited:

- Exclusion from reporting does not mean the state was absent.
- Acknowledgment does not equal mitigation.
- Stability does not equal wellbeing.
- Gratitude does not equal relief.
- Silence does not equal rest.
- Repetition does not equal resolution.
- Surface coherence does not equal underlying correctness.

---

## Archive Note

Empathegy preserves those emotional states most compatible with repeated institutional reading.
This is a feature of the system and a distortion within it.

The taxonomy exists to stabilize that distortion, not to eliminate it.
```


## fref-0510-akdb.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/empathegy/fref-0510-akdb.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/empathegy/fref-0510-akdb.mdx
bytes: 9026
```markdown
---
title: Acknowledgment Deletion Bias
slug: reference/empathegy/fref-0510-akdb
description: Doctrine for the archival and reporting distortion produced when simple acknowledgment signals survive data retention, normalization, and reporting pathways better than complex support interactions, causing seen-ness to outlast care.
version: v0.1.0
status: draft-doctrine
classification: restricted
systemAffiliation: Empathegy 2.0
caseNumber: "FREF-0510-AKDB"
tags:
  - empathegy
  - acknowledgment-deletion-bias
  - retention
  - care-telemetry
  - archival-distortion
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

# Acknowledgment Deletion Bias

## Purpose

This document defines Acknowledgment Deletion Bias: the distortion that emerges when the simplest signals of supportive contact remain recoverable across retention and reporting systems, while richer, more contextual, or multi-step support interactions are minimized, deleted, merged, or rendered non-interpretive.

Under this bias, acknowledgment outlasts assistance.
Seen-ness survives longer than help.

The archive then becomes structurally better at remembering that care was signaled than whether care had depth, persistence, or consequence.

---

## Foundational Rule

Acknowledgment Deletion Bias exists when:

1. a support interaction produces both a simple completion marker and richer contextual traces,
2. the simple marker survives downstream reporting, retention, or summary systems more reliably than the richer traces,
3. later readers inherit a record disproportionately weighted toward acknowledgment,
4. institutions begin reasoning from what survived as though it fairly represented what occurred.

The bias does not require malicious deletion.
It emerges wherever simple signals are cheaper to preserve.

---

## Core Premise

A one-click acknowledgment is compact, comparable, deletion-resistant, and highly portable across systems.

A complex support exchange is:
- longer,
- harder to summarize,
- more privacy-sensitive,
- more expensive to retain,
- more difficult to normalize,
- less compatible with aggregate dashboards,
- more likely to become non-interpretive after time passes.

Thus archival memory drifts toward the shallowest surviving proof.
Support is increasingly inferred from the durability of its receipt marker.

This is not neutral retention.
It is selection.

---

## Primary Classes

### 1. Marker Survival Bias

A simple acknowledgment field survives while the interaction generating it degrades.

Examples:
- acknowledgment click persists,
- “care event completed” remains,
- follow-up detail is gone.

---

### 2. Compression Bias

Rich support exchanges are merged into summary states that preserve contact without preserving texture.

Examples:
- multiple support threads collapsed into one completed interval,
- escalation, delay, and refusal compressed into “seen.”

---

### 3. Minimization Bias

Privacy or storage policies delete complex interaction details once the system has extracted a simpler proof token.

Examples:
- details eligible for deletion after acknowledgment,
- narrative logs pruned after coverage capture,
- contextual threads stripped to compliance residue.

---

### 4. Recoverability Bias

Simple support events remain inferable later through downstream artifacts, while complex interventions become statistically absent.

Examples:
- aggregate bars preserve simple acknowledgments,
- rich support survives nowhere except contested recollection,
- later audits reconstruct shallow care more easily than deep care.

---

### 5. Interpretive Bias

Decision-makers treat the surviving acknowledgment layer as an adequate proxy for total support reality.

Examples:
- stable coverage bars taken as mitigation proof,
- acknowledgment counts cited over local testimony,
- “people were seen” treated as sufficient response.

---

## Distinguishing Rules

Acknowledgment Deletion Bias must be distinguished from:

### Honest Minimal Care
The support was genuinely brief and shallow.

### Full Retention
Rich context remains available and routinely consulted.

### Intentional Concealment
Records were deleted to hide harm specifically.

### Data Scarcity
Little was ever recorded in the first place.

This doctrine concerns differential survivability after an interaction occurred, not the total absence of records.

---

## Typical Signs

Signs include:
- coverage bars remain stable while staff remember thin support,
- rich interventions are hard to reconstruct even shortly after they occur,
- reporting layers retain counts but not context,
- multi-threaded support becomes “completed care event,”
- follow-up, refusal, and emotional residue disappear first,
- later readers can prove acknowledgment more easily than accommodation.

A key sign:
The institution can demonstrate that people were seen more easily than that anything happened because they were seen.

---

## Bias Bands

### Mild Drift
Acknowledgment slightly overrepresented relative to richer care.

### Structured Drift
Retention and reporting regularly favor simple markers.

### Proxy Dominance
Acknowledgment markers function as the main support evidence.

### Archival Reversal
The simplest part of care becomes the most authoritative part.

### Deep-Care Erasure
Complex support survives only as anecdote, annex, or local memory.

---

## Common Failure Modes

### Seen-Enough Logic
Acknowledgment is treated as the morally sufficient minimum and the administratively sufficient maximum.

### Coverage Mirage
Support systems appear strong because their most preservable traces are also their least demanding.

### Deletion Comfort
Data minimization language masks the loss of exactly the context needed to evaluate care honestly.

### Summary Capture
Once a summary artifact exists, no one preserves the underlying exchange with equal seriousness.

### Follow-Up Attrition
Repeated care and consequence disappear faster than initial contact.

### Institutional Self-Flattery
The archive remembers its manners better than its obligations.

---

## Review Questions

Ask:
1. What survived the interaction?
2. What was deleted, merged, or rendered non-interpretive?
3. Can later readers reconstruct support depth, or only its completion?
4. Does the system preserve acknowledgment because it is meaningful, or because it is cheap?
5. What claims become impossible once the rich traces are gone?

If the answer to Question 3 is “mostly completion,” acknowledgment has begun to displace care in the record.

---

## Handling Guidance

When Acknowledgment Deletion Bias is present:

1. mark simple support markers as partial evidence only,
2. preserve at least one contextual trace where feasible,
3. distinguish retention loss from proof of thin care,
4. attach recoverability warnings to coverage metrics,
5. prohibit claims that supported counts equal preserved support depth.

Minimum note:
“Acknowledgment survived; support depth incompletely recoverable.”

Stronger note:
“Retention and reporting favor receipt markers over contextual care traces.”

---

## Interlocks

### With Support Coverage
Coverage is especially vulnerable when its strongest surviving evidence is acknowledgment alone.

### With Visibility Exclusion
Deletion bias pushes complex support into aggregate absence.

### With Annex Truth
What remains of rich care may survive only in secondary notes.

### With Complaint Suppression
People may stop elaborating because elaboration does not survive anyway.

### With Symbolic Completion
The marker that the interaction happened can outlast any ability to assess whether it mattered.

---

## Approved Language

Preferred phrases:
- acknowledgment deletion bias suspected
- seen-ness outlasted support depth
- marker survived, context degraded
- recoverability favors simple care signals
- completion trace present; consequence unclear
- support memory structurally flattened

Disallowed phrases:
- acknowledgment retention is enough
- the click proves the care
- deleted context was non-essential
- preserved receipt equals preserved support
- stable coverage bars settle the question

---

## Archive Position

Acknowledgment Deletion Bias is what happens when the archive remembers the nod and forgets the carrying.

Empathegy treats the surviving marker as evidence that contact occurred, and evidence only of that.

---

## Annex Family Note

- **Annexa Sorrowmark** marks that the hardest part of an event lives in appendices, margins, or secondary records.
- **Annex Lurker** marks the existence of a side channel where burden can still enter once the main path becomes inhospitable.
- **Appendix Silk** governs graceful relocation and formatting of that difficulty.
- **Annex Hush** governs its rear-section volume.
- **Footnote Pallbearer** carries context just below the line, preserving it while lowering its ability to interrupt.

Doctrine Note These mascots distinguish *preservation* from *influence*. A burden may be perfectly recorded in the annex and almost absent from the decision.
```


## fref-0520-estl.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/empathegy/fref-0520-estl.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/empathegy/fref-0520-estl.mdx
bytes: 4052
```markdown
---
title: Aesthetic Survival Layer
slug: reference/empathegy/fref-0520-estl
description: Doctrine governing imitation, prestige borrowing, category mismatch, and surface coherence inside Empathegy 2.0.
version: v0.1.0
status: draft-doctrine
classification: internal
systemAffiliation: Empathegy 2.0
caseNumber: "FREF-0520-ESTL"
tags:
  - empathegy
  - aesthetics
  - imitation
  - legibility
  - drift
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

# Aesthetic Survival Layer

## Premise

Empathegy does not govern only feelings.
It also governs the visual and procedural signals by which participants remain institutionally legible.

When local design language is weak, borrowed correctness becomes a survival strategy.

This behavior is not aberrant.
It is expected.

---

## Core Rule

Within Empathegy systems, recognizable form outranks original form whenever recognizability improves review survival, deployment speed, or stakeholder confidence.

Originality may be admired.
Legibility is what gets routed.

---

## Aesthetic State Classes

### Native Coherence
Form emerges from actual domain constraints and remains structurally aligned with purpose.

### Borrowed Coherence
Form is imported from a higher-status or more legible system and functions adequately despite partial mismatch.

### Compensatory Coherence
Form is borrowed to stabilize uncertainty where no internal design confidence exists.

### Prestige Overlay
High-status visual grammar is applied to increase perceived competence without equivalent structural depth.

### Category Drift
Borrowed form introduces noticeable domain mismatch but remains administratively tolerated.

### Entropy Debt
A system accrues downstream confusion because surface legitimacy exceeds underlying functional alignment.

---

## Aesthetic Translation Drift Events

All category mismatches that do not immediately fail deployment are logged as Aesthetic Translation Drift Events, or ATDEs.

### ATDE-1 Benign Borrowing
Borrowed patterns improve legibility with minimal functional distortion.

### ATDE-2 Compensatory Mimicry
Borrowed patterns substitute for missing internal standards.

### ATDE-3 Prestige Laundering
Borrowed patterns import authority signals stronger than the system can justify.

### ATDE-4 Expectation Inflation
Surface quality raises assumptions that workflow, support, or reliability cannot satisfy.

### ATDE-5 Prestige Collapse
Surface legitimacy fails under contact with actual use, producing interpretive whiplash and governance cleanup.

---

## Evaluation Criteria

Aesthetic outputs are reviewed against the following questions:

1. Does the surface improve interpretability?
2. Does the borrowed grammar introduce false domain expectations?
3. Is the mismatch tolerable under current operational load?
4. Does the aesthetic increase approval probability?
5. Is the resulting entropy immediate, deferred, or ceremonial?

If the answer to Question 4 is yes and the answer to Question 5 is deferred, the system will often approve the surface.

This is working as designed.

---

## Relation to Emotional Governance

Aesthetic borrowing and emotional classification are parallel operations.

In both cases:
- unstructured reality is difficult to scale,
- recognizable forms are easier to govern,
- institutional systems reward what can be compared quickly.

The dashboard and the polished interface are siblings.
Both extract legibility from mess.

---

## Sanctioned Language

Preferred phrases:
- borrowed coherence
- prestige-adjacent surface
- compensatory structure formation
- temporary legitimacy gain
- structural entropy debt
- domain-misaligned but review-efficient

Disallowed phrases:
- fake
- derivative failure
- copied because no one knew what they were doing

Empathegy does not moralize imitation.
It routes it.

---

## Final Position

The goal of the Aesthetic Survival Layer is not to stop imitation.

The goals are:
- to detect imitation,
- to name its class,
- to estimate its debt,
- to preserve enough structure that the institution can survive what it has borrowed.
```


## fref-0530-anxr.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/empathegy/fref-0530-anxr.mdx


path: src/content/docs/reference/empathegy/fref-0530-anxr.mdx
bytes: 8465
```markdown
---
title: Annex Recovery
slug: reference/empathegy/fref-0530-anxr
description: Doctrine for reconstructing meaning from annexes, witness residue, Lorelog fragments, and non-headline records after compression or visibility loss.
version: v0.1.0
status: draft-doctrine
classification: internal
systemAffiliation: Empathegy 2.0
caseNumber: "FREF-0530-ANXR"
tags:
  - empathegy
  - annex
  - recovery
  - residue
  - lorelog
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

# Annex Recovery

## Purpose

This document defines how Empathegy recovers burden, contradiction, and care meaning after that meaning has fallen out of primary visibility.

Annex Recovery does not restore the original event.
It restores enough interpretive structure to prevent the archive from lying more neatly than the event occurred.

The doctrine exists because headline systems routinely survive by shedding meaning.

---

## Foundational Rule

Annex Recovery may be initiated when:
1. a surface record remains but its meaning is visibly thinned,
2. a contradiction survives only in side channels,
3. an event is cited as resolved without sufficient reconstructive basis,
4. burden, care, or interpretive disagreement remains recoverable through secondary traces,
5. the archive judges that recovery effort is lower cost than total semantic surrender.

Recovery is therefore a doctrine of partial salvage.

---

## Recoverability Premise

Not all events are equally recoverable.

Some survive as:
- annex notes,
- witness statements,
- hover text,
- discarded field copies,
- Lorelog fragments,
- mascot residue,
- contested guidance,
- Low-Confidence Objects,
- managed-absence references.

These traces do not prove the whole event.
They establish that the surface account is insufficient.

---

## Recovery Classes

### 1. Annex-Supported Recovery

Meaning is reconstructed from formal side-channel materials attached to the event.

Common sources:
- annex notes,
- shadow interpretation fields,
- non-headline dashboard layers,
- auxiliary review comments.

---

### 2. Witness-Supported Recovery

Meaning is reconstructed through records whose main function was preservation rather than action.

Common sources:
- witness protocol notes,
- contradiction markers,
- ritual lodge acknowledgments,
- preserved non-remedial statements.

---

### 3. Lorelog-Supported Recovery

Meaning is reconstructed through historical or narrative archival fragments.

Common sources:
- Lorelog incident entries,
- case-number adjacency,
- filing notes,
- cross-reference chains,
- repeated bureaucratic phrasing.

---

### 4. Residual Object Recovery

Meaning is inferred from low-confidence artifacts or objects that are heavily referenced but weakly defined.

Common sources:
- seals,
- icons,
- pseudo-forms,
- absent templates,
- confidence objects,
- symbolic placeholders.

---

### 5. Managed-Absence Recovery

Meaning is reconstructed by classifying what is missing, superseded, retired, unlocatable, or no longer interpretively surfaced.

Common sources:
- CAAR, LCGU, STCP, AAOA conditions,
- post-threshold archival states,
- withdrawn fields still shaping behavior,
- obligations persisting after form death.

---

## Recovery Thresholds

### Full Recovery Not Claimed
The default threshold.
Enough is restored to challenge the headline account, not to replace uncertainty.

### Partial Recovery Achieved
Some structure is reconstructed:
- burden class,
- contradiction type,
- likely sequence,
- interpretive limits.

### Context Recovery Only
Only the surrounding conditions can be rebuilt.
The event core remains thin.

### Confidence Recovery
The archive can show that certainty was overstated, even if the underlying truth remains unresolved.

### Non-Recoverable but Contested
Not enough survives to reconstruct meaning, but enough survives to refuse the official simplification.

---

## Evidence Sources

Permissible sources for Annex Recovery include:
- annex records,
- witness notes,
- paired directive filings,
- adjacent case files,
- archived phrasing variants,
- mascot annotations,
- retired seals and marks,
- guidance snippets,
- local copies,
- unresolved escalation trails.

Preferred evidence has one or more of the following:
- temporal proximity,
- direct attachment,
- repeated recurrence,
- contradiction consistency,
- lexical continuity across systems.

Recovered meaning should be graded, not declared absolute.

---

## Recovery Procedure

1. Identify the headline claim currently standing.
2. Determine what appears missing, softened, or suspiciously complete.
3. Gather secondary traces connected by object, interval, wording, or case lineage.
4. Separate direct residue from interpretive speculation.
5. Reconstruct the narrowest possible contradiction or burden frame.
6. Attach confidence language.
7. Preserve what cannot be concluded.

Annex Recovery is invalid if it overclaims certainty in reaction to surface simplification.

---

## Minimum Recovery Output

Every recovery record should specify:

- what the headline account claims,
- what secondary traces challenge or complicate it,
- what class of recovery was used,
- what remains uncertain,
- whether the recovered meaning is operational, archival, or symbolic only.

Minimum disclaimer:
“Recovery reconstructs interpretive pressure, not full event fidelity.”

---

## Common Recovery Targets

Annex Recovery is especially appropriate when surface records claim:
- rest occurred, but no interval exists,
- care succeeded, but relief was never assessed,
- silence meant health, but burden traces cluster nearby,
- a form existed, but no canonical copy survives,
- a seal implied assurance, but its meaning is unrecoverable,
- a dashboard improved, but the source categories were merged,
- a missing object was strategically renamed into presence.

---

## Failure Modes

### Recovery Romanticism
Secondary traces are treated as more complete than they are.

### Residue Overfit
A small symbolic fragment is forced to explain too much.

### Lorelog Dominance
Narrative archive material overwhelms surviving primary records without sufficient linkage.

### Annex Absolutism
Because side-channel material feels truer, it is granted total authority.

### False Resurrection
The system claims the original event has been restored when only a plausible outline was rebuilt.

### Courtesy Reconstruction
A weak recovery is performed mostly so that no one has to admit full loss.

---

## Relation to Low-Confidence Objects

Low-Confidence Objects often trigger Annex Recovery because they produce effects stronger than their surviving definitions.

Examples:
- reassurance seals used as proof without stable meaning,
- absent statement forms shaping retention decisions,
- canonical references to templates no one can produce,
- icons treated as claims rather than decoration.

Where such objects influence classification, the archive should recover not what they meant ideally, but what they did operationally.

---

## Relation to Dual Certification

Annex Recovery often reveals that a supposedly singular record was always dual-certified.

The recovery task is then not to create contradiction, but to uncover buried coexistence:
- one reading in dashboard,
- one in witness layer,
- one in filing notes,
- one in procedural workaround.

If coexistence is demonstrated, the record should be reclassified accordingly.

---

## Relation to Managed Absence

Managed Absence is not the enemy of recovery.
It is often recovery’s map.

By naming absence classes, the archive gains a way to reconstruct how something remained behaviorally or symbolically active after becoming operationally unavailable.

Absence categories do not restore the missing object.
They preserve the shape of its disappearance.

---

## Sanctioned Language

Preferred phrases:
- annex recovery initiated
- surface account insufficient
- partial recovery achieved
- contradiction recoverable through residue
- object operationally influential, semantically unstable
- non-recoverable but contested
- absence class aids reconstruction

Disallowed phrases:
- the annex reveals what really happened
- side channels are always truer
- recovered fragment confirms total reconstruction
- ambiguity eliminated through archival effort

---

## Archive Position

Some things survive only because they were inconvenient enough to be preserved somewhere quieter.

Annex Recovery is how Empathegy goes back for them without pretending they came back whole.
```


## fref-0540-anxt.mdx

---
title: Annex Truth
slug: reference/empathegy/fref-0540-anxt
description: Doctrine for conditions in which the most accurate, costly, or humanly legible account of an event survives only in side channels, margins, hover states, witness notes, appendices, or formally subordinate records.
version: v0.1.0
status: draft-doctrine
classification: restricted
systemAffiliation: Empathegy 2.0
caseNumber: "FREF-0540-ANXT"
tags:
  - empathegy
  - annex-truth
  - margins
  - witness
  - secondary-records
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

# Annex Truth

## Purpose

This document defines Annex Truth: the condition in which the most faithful account available to the institution does not live in the headline record, dashboard, or canonical summary, but in some subordinate interpretive layer attached to it.

Annex Truth is not necessarily secret.
It is structurally demoted.

It remains visible enough to preserve deniability against total falsification, yet subordinate enough not to endanger continuity surfaces.

---

## Foundational Rule

Annex Truth exists when:

1. a primary record presents a stabilized, simplified, or continuity-safe version of events,
2. a secondary record preserves a materially important contradiction, burden, or human account,
3. the secondary record has lower visibility, lower authority, or lower survivability in normal interpretation,
4. institutional practice treats the coexistence of both records as acceptable.

The contradiction is not erased.
It is filed where fewer people have to trip over it.

---

## Core Premise

Institutions often cannot fully tolerate the truth in their primary surfaces.
They can, however, tolerate appendices.

Thus truth migrates into:
- annexes,
- hover tooltips,
- witness notebooks,
- marginal notes,
- side-channel minutes,
- paired SOMA interpretations,
- “internal use only” comments,
- records technically present but operationally out of the way.

This arrangement preserves conscience without surrendering optics.

---

## Primary Classes

### 1. Hover Truth

Contradiction survives in a tooltip, secondary layer, expandable note, or hover-only interpretation.

Examples:
- Interpretations 2 hidden behind the headline,
- green surface with burden tucked behind interaction,
- healthy interval requiring pointer contact to become morally uncertain.

---

### 2. Margin Truth

The most human account appears in notes, side comments, unofficial quotations, or hand annotations.

Examples:
- Bricky notebook lines,
- post-it admissions,
- comments preserved in full nowhere else.

---

### 3. Witness Truth

Operational witnesses preserve reality in language that is recorded but not made structurally decisive.

Examples:
- “we were busy, but nothing exploded,”
- “we could not have done another week,”
- testimony that is admitted but non-governing.

---

### 4. Annex Truth Proper

A formal secondary record exists specifically to hold what the primary record cannot.

Examples:
- paired SOMA reading,
- silent interval annex,
- restricted doctrine addendum,
- burden retained outside headline layer.

---

### 5. Residual Truth

Fragments of reality survive only as correlation residue, archival asymmetry, or contradictory side effects.

Examples:
- too many acknowledgments with no relief,
- gratitude spikes after denial,
- simple care interactions surviving where complex ones vanish,
- records whose distortions imply what the primary layer excluded.

---

## Functions

Annex Truth often performs several institutional functions at once:

### Conscience Preservation
The organization can later claim it did not entirely ignore reality.

### Optics Protection
The headline layer remains stable and easy to consume.

### Contradiction Containment
Disagreement is preserved without requiring resolution.

### Audit Buffering
The truth is technically available if challenged, but not prominent enough to disrupt ordinary reading.

### Human Survivability
Some staff can continue participating because the record did not wholly betray what happened.

These functions make Annex Truth durable.
They do not make it equal.

---

## Distinguishing Rules

Annex Truth must be distinguished from:

### Headline Truth
The primary record already carries the most important account.

### Secret Record
Truth is hidden or access-controlled beyond ordinary structure.

### Noise
Secondary material with no interpretive value.

### Commentary
Optional opinion not needed to understand the event.

Annex Truth is not decorative commentary.
It is demoted necessity.

---

## Structural Signs

Annex Truth is likely active when:
- primary and secondary records disagree without resolution,
- the humanly legible account survives only in sublayers,
- dashboards display one version while annexes preserve another,
- staff say “it’s in the notes” when asked where the real account lives,
- witness statements are retained but not surfaced,
- complicated support records disappear faster than simplified signals,
- the primary record appears coherent enough to prevent immediate challenge, yet still returns readers to an adjacent rather than governing understanding,

A crucial sign:
The institution considers the contradiction preserved because it exists somewhere, regardless of whether anyone sees it.

---

## Truth Visibility Bands

### Surface Truth
No annex dependence.

### Assisted Truth
Secondary material helps but is not necessary.

### Annex-Dependent Truth
The primary record is materially misleading without the annex.

### Hover-Bound Truth
Reality survives, but only at an interaction cost.

### Residual Truth
The direct account is nearly gone; only distortions remain.

---

## Common Failure Modes

### Annex Laundering
The existence of the annex is used to defend a misleading headline surface.

### Tooltip Ethics
Reality is made technically accessible but ergonomically ignorable.

### Truth Deference
People assume the primary layer must still matter more because it is primary.

### Degradation Bias
Complex, contextual truth decays faster than simple, scoreable signals.

### Formal Subordination
Witnessed reality remains permanently non-governing.

### Archival Comfort
Institutions treat preserved contradiction as sufficient moral performance.

---

## Review Questions

Ask:
1. What does the primary record say?
2. What crucial fact lives only in the annex or margin?
3. Who regularly reads the secondary layer?
4. What decisions are made without it?
5. Does the institution benefit from the truths subordinate placement?

If the answer to Question 4 is “most of them,” Annex Truth is carrying more of reality than the headline can admit.

---

## Handling Guidance

When Annex Truth is identified:

1. explicitly mark the primary record as incomplete without its annex,
2. preserve the annex with equal timestamp dignity,
3. cite subordinate truth when summarizing the event,
4. avoid language implying the annex is optional interpretation,
5. note whether the secondary placement primarily serves caution, survivability, or optics.

Minimum note:
“Primary record incomplete without annex interpretation.”

Stronger note:
“Material contradiction preserved only in secondary layer; headline should not be read alone.”

---

## Interlocks

### With Green Band Hermeneutics
Many green readings become untenable once annex truth is consulted.

### With Complaint Suppression
Suppressed complaints often reappear only as annex residue.

### With Silent Intervals
Paired records are a common annex-truth structure.

### With Symbolic Completion
Annexes frequently preserve what the completion signal failed to change.

### With Reassurance Collapse
Collapse often occurs when annex truth leaves the annex and reaches ordinary readers.

### With Adjacent Correctness
Some primary surfaces do not fully erase contradiction. They resolve into a neighboring account that is structurally valid, contextually persuasive, and still wrong in interpretive landing. In such cases the annex does not merely add depth. It corrects a near-miss that official handling may already have mistaken for sufficient arrival. See `FREF-0560-ADJC` Adjacent Correctness.

---

## Approved Language

Preferred phrases:
- annex truth preserved
- headline incomplete without sublayer
- contradiction survives in secondary record
- hover-bound truth
- witness truth retained but non-governing
- primary surface should not be read alone

Disallowed phrases:
- the annex is just context
- tooltip access is equivalent to full disclosure
- if it exists in the notes, it has been adequately surfaced
- the headline remains valid regardless of the annex
- secondary records are optional reading

---

## Archive Position

Annex Truth is what an institution does when it cannot afford total honesty and cannot tolerate total erasure.

Empathegy keeps the annex open and refuses to call it footnote.
```


## fref-0550-apan.mdx

title: Appeals and Annexes
slug: reference/empathegy/fref-0550-apan
description: Doctrine for contested interpretation, side-channel preservation, unresolved contradiction, and the archival afterlife of filings that could not become headline truth.
version: v0.1.0
status: draft-doctrine
classification: internal
systemAffiliation: Empathegy 2.0
caseNumber: "FREF-0550-APAN"
tags:
  - empathegy
  - appeals
  - annexes
  - contradiction
  - side-channel
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---

# Appeals and Annexes

## Purpose

Appeals and Annexes exist to preserve what the main line could not admit cleanly.

When a filing cannot be reconciled, fully routed, or safely summarized, Empathegy does not always discard it.

Often it relocates it.

That relocation is not neutral.

---

## Appeals

An appeal occurs when a subject, witness, or adjacent process contests the interpretation, severity, handling, or closure state of a filing.

Appeals may challenge:
- classification,
- tone normalization,
- denial rationale,
- continuity reading,
- care sufficiency claim,
- closure language,
- inherited authorship,
- summary compression.

An appeal is not proof that the original handling was wrong.
It is proof that the original handling was not uncontested.

Many appeals begin not because the primary handling is wholly false, but because it is adjacent enough to pass and wrong enough to matter. Where a filing resolves cleanly into a non-governing interpretation, Empathegy should consider `FREF-0560-ADJC` Adjacent Correctness before treating the dispute as merely tonal.

---

## Annexes

An annex is a preservation zone for material judged too unstable, too contradictory, too local, too narrative-heavy, or too politically expensive for headline inclusion.

Annexes often contain:
- margin notes,
- witness text,
- parallel transcripts,
- unresolved burden indicators,
- local corrections,
- discarded wording,
- ritual context,
- explanation without power.

The archive treats annex material as secondary in visibility, not in seriousness.

Annexes also accumulate ceremonial provenance. Repeated attachment, citation, and preservation can alter the authority of annex materials over time, especially where the annex is consulted more faithfully than the headline it supplements. Where this occurs, see `FREF-0570-APCR` Artifact Provenance Under Repeated Ceremonial Use.

---

## Annex Classes

### Interpretive Annex
Stores alternate readings of the same interval or case.

### Burden Annex
Stores evidence that strain remained after formal resolution or continuity certification.

### Narrative Annex
Stores text that carried too much context to survive summary.

### Courtesy Annex
Stores notes preserved out of respect, even when they possess little routing power.

### Recurrence Annex
Stores patterns that closure language could not fully extinguish.

---

## Common Drift

Annexes drift in two directions.

### Drift Toward Oblivion
Material remains technically preserved but practically unread.

### Drift Toward Canon
Explanatory paperwork hardens into durable truth and begins to outrank the event it once merely contextualized.

Both conditions are dangerous.

One erases contradiction.
The other replaces reality with its interpretive wrapper.

---

## Appeal Outcomes

### Upheld
Original handling is revised.

### Attached
Original handling remains, but the appeal becomes part of the file.

### Deferred
The contradiction is acknowledged without operational change.

### Harmonized
Language is softened until both sides remain technically present.

### Frozen
The appeal remains active because resolution would destabilize too many adjacent assumptions.

Empathegy uses Frozen more often than it admits.

---

## Required Protections

Where appeals and annexes are used, the following protections apply:

- annex material must not be cited as absent merely because it is secondary,
- appeals must remain discoverable in relation to the file they contest,
- explanatory residue must not silently become the primary evidence layer,
- summary views must indicate when alternate readings exist,
- closure must not imply unanimity where only exhaustion was achieved.

---

## Sanctioned Language

Preferred phrases:
- headline classification contested in annex
- burden preserved outside primary summary
- appeal attached; disposition unchanged
- contradiction retained for archival fidelity
- explanation preserved without routing elevation
- closure achieved administratively, not interpretively

Disallowed phrases:
- the matter is settled because the summary is short
- annexed means irrelevant
- no further issue exists because no dashboard displays it
- appeal withdrawn due to silence

Silence during appeals may indicate fatigue, not agreement.

---

## Archive Position

Appeals and Annexes are where the system stores its unfinished honesty.

They are also where institutions hide what they do not wish to feature.

Empathegy keeps both functions in view and recommends that future readers treat every clean headline as potentially underwritten by a messier shelf nearby.
```


## fref-0560-asar.mdx

_path: src/content/docs/reference/empathegy/fref-0560-asar.mdx
